<span id="freeTextContainer16232253313813738045">Unlike a lot of my Animorphs 2-star reviews, I do remember this one. It's a choose-your-own-adventure story. Mostly I remember choosing routes where I die a lot, then finding the happy ending and reading the story backwards from there. Probably not the best way to enjoy one of these types of books.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1125437710">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1125437710" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1914201-josiah" class="left imgcol" title="Josiah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1239682454p2/1914201.jpg" alt="Josiah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1125437710?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 07, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1914201-josiah" class="user" title="Josiah">Josiah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1125437710">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12767192818708826620"> If the name on the cover belongs to the actual author of this book, then <em>The First Journey</em>, to the best of my knowledge, is the first gamebook in history to be written by a Newbery Medalist. Yes, Katherine Applegate, author of <em>The One and Only Ivan</em>, was chief literary architect of the <em>Animorphs</em> empire, years before the Newbery committee awarded her its coveted top prize, and alongside the main <em>Animorphs</em> series were several offshoots. Was Katherine Applegate the real author of the two-book <em>Animo</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12767192818708826620"> If the name on the cover belongs to the actual author of this book, then <em>The First Journey</em>, to the best of my knowledge, is the first gamebook in history to be written by a Newbery Medalist. Yes, Katherine Applegate, author of <em>The One and Only Ivan</em>, was chief literary architect of the <em>Animorphs</em> empire, years before the Newbery committee awarded her its coveted top prize, and alongside the main <em>Animorphs</em> series were several offshoots. Was Katherine Applegate the real author of the two-book <em>Animorphs: Alternamorphs</em> addendum, or were they ghostwritten, to give her a break after the effort she put into writing the primary series? We may never know the answer for sure, though I could ask her about it if I ever meet her at another bookstore event. I would be quite interested in learning if <em>Alternamorphs</em> was her work. <br /><br /> "Because sometimes the stuff you see in the movies, the stuff you thought could never, ever happen to you...well, it <em>can</em> happen. It <em>does</em> happen. I've seen it."<br /><br /> —<em>The First Journey</em>, from the Introduction<br /><br /> For fans of <em>Animorphs</em>, the background for <em>The First Journey</em> is already well-known, but a short introductory piece is included for those of us without prior <em>Animorphs</em> experience. You initially are an outsider to the regular group of Animorph kids—Jake, Marco, Cassie, Rachel and Tobias—but your desire for a little late-night skateboarding puts you in position to witness a bizarre alien creature come and ask the Animorphs for help. Your assistance is requested, as well. The Andalite race is in serious trouble from the predatory Hork-Bajir aliens, and so is humanity. Desperate for all the help he can muster, the Andalite leader endows you with the same Animorph power your five new friends have, before he meets a grim fate at the hands of the enemy. You and the more experienced Animorphs must flee the initial extermination attempt of the Hork-Bajir, then circle back and infiltrate its legions to prevent them from overrunning the planet. You'll have the exact same Animorphing power at your disposal as the other five, but choose your morphs cautiously: selecting the wrong animal in this book leads to swift death. Messing with animal DNA is serious stuff. To survive your battle with predatory aliens, you'll need cunning, intelligence, and some good luck, plus the knowhow to work effectively with your Animorph compatriots, understanding one another's strengths and weaknesses and how to utilize them to save the world. Can you do what it takes to band together and decisively repel the extraterrestrial menace? <br /><br /> This beginning to the <em>Alternamorphs</em> miniseries features some unusual game elements worth noting. For starters, the book has only one ending, if it can be called that; it just kind of drifts off into nothingness on page one hundred nine, leaving readers to assume the end has been reached. While many choice intersections offer three decisions, only one is ever the correct animal to morph into; any other choice soon ends with a grisly death or lifetime sentence trapped in the body of the animal you became, at which point you're instructed to turn back to your last decision and try again. The story elements often confused me, and there were a few continuity errors in the text, too. I'm not sure the narrative made perfect linear sense, either. I can't say <em>The First Journey</em> isn't a difficult gamebook, however; the logic behind the right choice to be made at each juncture teeters perilously close to pure randomness, and it would take almost a miracle to make it successfully to the end on one's first attempt. If you do, congratulations: you're a better gamebook player than I. Well, a luckier one, at least. <br /><br /> What's my verdict on the first <em>Alternamorphs</em> installment? I have to believe it was a ghostwriter, not Katherine Applegate, who penned this paperback (Tonya Alicia Martin, perhaps? I've seen places online that credit her as the ghostwriter). Still, there are glimmers of interestingness, and it's a fun story if one isn't expecting too much from it, either as a gamebook or a middle-grade novel. I'm sure the main series is superior, but fans who can't get enough of the <em>Animorphs</em> universe may enjoy interacting in these gamebooks with the characters they already know so well. If you want to find out what the <em>Animorphs</em> books are really like, though, start with the main series. That's the place to begin if you want to see what a talented writer Katherine Applegate can be. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12767192818708826620">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1020018444">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1020018444" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/24009998-julie-decker" class="left imgcol" title="Julie Decker"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442960946p2/24009998.jpg" alt="Julie Decker" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1020018444?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 07, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/24009998-julie-decker" class="user" title="Julie Decker">Julie Decker</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1020018444">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3956107442993619524">THIS IS A CHOOSE-YOUR-OWN-ADVENTURE-STYLE <em>ANIMORPHS BOOK</em>. IT IS NOT PART OF THE CANON (and, as a personal aside, is not recommended by me). The book allows you, the reader, to "become" part of the Animorphs by putting you there when Elfangor lands and allowing you to acquire the morphing power, then presenting you with a series of decisions (choose-your-own adventure style) to dictate the plot. Story elements of the first book and the eleventh book are incorporated, allowing the reader to partic</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3956107442993619524">THIS IS A CHOOSE-YOUR-OWN-ADVENTURE-STYLE <em>ANIMORPHS BOOK</em>. IT IS NOT PART OF THE CANON (and, as a personal aside, is not recommended by me). The book allows you, the reader, to "become" part of the Animorphs by putting you there when Elfangor lands and allowing you to acquire the morphing power, then presenting you with a series of decisions (choose-your-own adventure style) to dictate the plot. Story elements of the first book and the eleventh book are incorporated, allowing the reader to participate in the first trip to the Yeerk pool with the Animorphs and a strange altered version of a second trip through the <em>Sario Rip</em> plot leading into the Amazon jungle. There is only one winning ending, which involves using accidental time travel to stop Visser Three from killing Visser One's host before Visser One entered the picture, and you get to eat pizza with Jake.<br /><br />Overall these are poorly conceived and pretty cheap. Not a necessary or enjoyable addition to the <em>Animorphs</em> universe.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3956107442993619524">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_59624898">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/59624898?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 14, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1197500-weathervane" class="user" title="Weathervane">Weathervane</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1197500-weathervane?shelf=animorphs" class="actionLinkLite">animorphs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer59624898">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4515955608532263783">Poor. The book manages to be mostly incoherent; nothing is explained properly. For instance, we start out at the first pool raid, but the second part of the book jumps way ahead to a point after Ax is found. The transition is very clumsy, and what's more, if you haven't read the books on which the two stories are based, you'll be entirely lost. I knew what was going on during the first section, but the second section was a complete mystery.<br /><br />The characters do not act like themselves; Ax actually s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4515955608532263783">Poor. The book manages to be mostly incoherent; nothing is explained properly. For instance, we start out at the first pool raid, but the second part of the book jumps way ahead to a point after Ax is found. The transition is very clumsy, and what's more, if you haven't read the books on which the two stories are based, you'll be entirely lost. I knew what was going on during the first section, but the second section was a complete mystery.<br /><br />The characters do not act like themselves; Ax actually says, "Cooler than my tail?" Yeah, no. That's not Ax. Your "character" basically has no relationships with the other Animorphs. You're just a cardboard cutout.<br /><br />The gamebook design is terrible. A choice either kills you or allows you to go on; there is no branching plot! The author obviously didn't understand what made gamebooks fun. It's not the blind trial-and-error. And the deaths -- oh, the deaths -- they're often shamefully stupid.<br /><br />Then there are the weird inconsistencies. Ax shrugs at one point -- out of character, of course, but on the very next page he shrugs again and it is suggested that it may have been his first use of the gesture. Are you kidding me? This is just lazy.<br /><br />Finally, add a decent share of typos to the list of faults.<br /><br />This book blows.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4515955608532263783">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15948161330320118835">I *really* should have listened to Jacqueline when she said the Alternamorphs were not worth reading. Yes, it's a choose-your-own adventure book, but I have good memories of them from high school, and yes, it tells the same story, but I liked them the first time around, right? So how bad can it be?<br /><br />BAD.<br /><br />The same story - actually TWO different books (about 150 pages each) - re-worded and paraphrased in places, so that *you* are the main character.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText15948161330320118835">I *really* should have listened to Jacqueline when she said the Alternamorphs were not worth reading. Yes, it's a choose-your-own adventure book, but I have good memories of them from high school, and yes, it tells the same story, but I liked them the first time around, right? So how bad can it be?<br /><br />BAD.<br /><br />The same story - actually TWO different books (about 150 pages each) - re-worded and paraphrased in places, so that *you* are the main character. It's all chopped up, diced and spliced, and reduced to a mere 115 pages. Also there is the assumption that you've read the original series (or seen the TV show) because there are whole parts that would leave someone new to the series befuddled &amp; confused. Even having read the series, I felt befuddled and confused.<br /><br />Had I not been bored out of my mind, with nothing else to do, I wouldn't have read more than 20 pages. I will not be reading the 2nd.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer134006705">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9676522352965959516">It's like "Choose Your Own Adventure" + "Animorphs." It's a bit disappointing compared to the original series. I wish "I" had more personality, though I know it's my decisions that would've shown "my" personality.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cJIurqmo44drBytvFYTzOyq4iw6EK5AgMsIQe4gcJoIVRhF9W3r3feffX9Rr5RWJY09IF83214pYyxXpRInQxw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1036736.Katherine_Applegate">About Katherine Applegate</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1036736.Katherine_Applegate"><img alt="1036736" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1269837168p2/1036736.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer9037724231898498431">Applegate was born in Michigan in 1956. Since then she has lived in Texas, Florida, California, Minnesota, Illinois, North Carolina, and after living in Pelago, Italy for a year, she has moved back to Southern California. She has an eleven year old son named Jake Mates, although she says the Animorph leader is not named after him. In 2003 she and her husband, Michael Grant, her co-author on many p</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9037724231898498431">Applegate was born in Michigan in 1956. Since then she has lived in Texas, Florida, California, Minnesota, Illinois, North Carolina, and after living in Pelago, Italy for a year, she has moved back to Southern California. She has an eleven year old son named Jake Mates, although she says the Animorph leader is not named after him. In 2003 she and her husband, Michael Grant, her co-author on many projects including Animorphs, adopted their daughter, Julia, in China.[citation needed] Following the end of Animorphs, Applegate took three years off. She is back at work and has written a picture book called "The Buffalo Storm," a middle reader novel called "Home of the Brave," and an early chapters series "Roscoe Riley Rules" with Harper Collins. Her book "Home of the Brave" has won the SCBWI Golden Kite Award, the Bank Street 2008 Josette Frank Award, and is a Judy Lopez Memorial Award honor book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9037724231898498431">...more</a>

    </div>
